text:
This recipe is FANTASTIC!!!  I have made it three/four times since I found it with different variations, though I am rating for the recipe itself.  Definitely 5 stars!!!  After reading through the reviews, please take into account the cooking time of each vegetable and adjust the size you cut them accordingly.  Suggestions to change it up would be:  1.)  Instead of plain olive oil, try the garlic olive oil - gives it a great taste.  2.)  Instead of olive oil, use Wishbone Italian dressing.  3.)  Add onions, whole garlic cloves and quartered mushrooms (must be quartered as whole mushrooms give off to much moisture).  4.)  Add Parmesan or Asiago cheese to the bread crumbs.  5.)  Change up the bread crumbs to the Italian variety - goes great with the Italian dressing.  6.)  Try panko crumbs or the Italian panko crumbs - which are fabulous in place of the bread crumbs.   Thanks Jana for submitting such a great and easy recipe!!!

text:
Ive made this a few times now, each with a slight variation.  Follow the exact recipe and i give it 4 stars.  A couple changes and its a 5 star dish!  My 5 star rendition...used seasoned breadcrumbs and bump it up to 2/3 cup...add a tablespoon or two more of olive oil to compensate for the additional breadcrumbs.  If you dont mind a few extra calories, throw in about 1/3 cup of freshly grated Parmesan cheese with the breadcrumbs.  Use red skinned potatoes...they have a more more desirable texture and a sweeter flavor that complements the zucchini much better.  Step up the Bell Pepper just a little too...either one large one or two smaller ones.  I like to add one green and one red for some extra variety.  After the potatoes are tender, i put the entire dish in the broiler for a minute or two to give everything a nice, even browning which gives it a VERY delicious crispy outside....just watch it closely...it will burn REALLY fast if you let it!  You just want a nice, even golden browning across the entire dish.  Toss and serve.

This recipe is so simple and soooo good!  Hard to believe you can get such a lovely flavor from so few ingredients.  I've made this several times now and really enjoy it - the kids, too!  I cut the veggies a bit smaller and spread them out to roast in a jelly roll pan, stirring occasionally - you can reduce the cooking time to 30-40 minutes with smaller pieces.  I've served this dish with fish, meat, chicken, whatever - it can't miss!

text:
A wonderful recipe, came out perfect! I made a few changes..I used Italian Breadcrumbs and added 1/4 cup of parmesan per others' suggestions (also omitted the paprika). I left the skin on the potatoes. I added an extra clove of garlic to the veggies. I also added a medium onion, large dice. Tossed all the veggies first in oil in a large ziplock, then in a separate ziplock, tossed the veggies in the breadcrumb mixture (tossed in two batches to ensure veggies were evenly coated). I am looking forward to making this again this weekend as a side dish for a BBQ!!

We really enjoyed this.  I didn't have any red pepper on hand, so I subbed red onion.  I also had some mushrooms that needed to be used up, so I added them as well.  The only suggestion that I would have is to start the potatoes about 20 minutes before the rest of the vegetables if you like your veggies crisp-tender.  This way the potatoes can be cooked through without overcooking the rest of the veggies.  Hubby liked it a lot too!  Thanks for the recipe.

One of my favorite ways to prepare veggies is roasting them, but I had never thought or heard of mixing bread crumbs in. Gives a really nice texture. Made a smaller batch and roasted in the toaster oven. I used granulated garlic instead of fresh because I thought fresh slices would burn. I also used lemon-pepper seasoning instead of paprika to better compliment the main dish, Parmesan Sage Pork Chops also on this site. Make sure the zucchini is in quite large pieces compared to the potatoes since zucchini cook much faster. Mine came out a little too mushy by the time the potatoes were golden (my fault, not the recipe's). I also added a carrot chunks since I had one to use up. Nice addition. I'll be doing this often!

This was pretty good. I used half an onion in place of the red pepper. I didn't have any fresh garlic on hand, so I used powdered, and while it was still tasty, I think fresh would have given a better flavor. I also didn't have any bread crumbs and didn't feel like making any, so I left them out, and added about a 1/3 cup of parmesan cheese. I used seasoned salt instead of paprika, and added some onion powder. I was a little worried about the temperature because my oven tends to cook hotter than others. So, I put it in at 350. Next time I will be sure and cook it on 400 because the potatoes weren't quite as cooked as we would have liked. The zucchini and onion were delicious, though. I think this would be superb with some asparagus and some lemon pepper. Bacon bits would be good in this too.

text:
Great recipe...not sure how somehow can say there was no flavour- unless one is cooking a  frozen veggies as vegetable on their own have a great summer flavour without even adding anything! This is a great recipe and easy to adjust  to your family's veggie preference ... 
I was making this a day ahead and was in a rush to make it all ready ....so I boiled the potatoes, and on a fry pan sauteed mushrooms on olive oil-added garlic, small carrots cut in round small pieces....once done added cut chunks of potatoes to turn gold-ish...added paprika as per recipe...but also some balsamic dressing...then added the zucchini I had yellow and green.I did not have any red peppers on hand. Once all done I transferred it all to a casserole dish , topped all with more bread crumbs and some feta and marble cheese...so its all ready to put in the oven the next day.. This is a great versatile recipe-it give a great base and ideas for your dish to adjust to your liking.

text:
I made it for my vegetarian daughter but all of us like this dish. I didn't realize that I was out of bread crumbs. Yikes!!! I was in the middle of the recipe with no time to stop and run to the store. I took some seasoned croutons, placed them in a zip lock bag, took my rolling pin, and rolled them into crumbs. I used them in the recipe, what a life saver, they turned out great. The only step I would do differently is add the zucchini after the dish has cooked for 30 minutes. I checked the dish half way through, and the zucchini looked awesome, but it still had a half hour to cook because of the potatoes, the zucchini was over cooked. Also, I tasted it half way through and it is bland so I added 1/4c of grated Parmesan cheese as many suggested by others. I will be making this again it is easy and good. My daughter the vegetarian gave a thumbs up.

text:
I knew before I ever started this recipe that the baking time of one hour was excessive for both my potatoes (I used smallish red skins) and the other veggies.  In fact the zucchini and bell pepper would have been total mush had they been baked for an hour.  However, I was still intrigued with this recipe, so I forged ahead, knowing I would have to make some major adjustments.  I scaled this way back for just the two of us, and used 1 T. panko, 1 T. Parmesan (as suggested by others), and the other seasonings.  I started with the potatoes, halving them and coating them with a little EVOO and some of my crumb mixture and baked on a baking sheet, flesh side down for about 30 minutes.  Coated the veggies with the remaining oil and crumbs and added them to the baking sheet with the potatoes.  At this point I turned my potatoes flesh side up.  Baked another 10-15 minutes for crisp-tender veggies.   While I loved the potatoes with the crumb mixture, I wasn‚Äôt wild about the veggies with the crumbs.  The crumbs on the potatoes were crisp, but soggy on the veggies.  Guess you could say I have a love/hate relationship with this recipe.  I‚Äôll make the potatoes again, but won‚Äôt be adding the veggies.

text:
MMMMMMmmmm!!! The best part about this recipe is that it is so quick, easy, and versatile. You can do some many variations. I followed the recipes exactly, but added in some onions (I LOVE onions), and a dash of Parmesan cheese.   But here's the trick to make it great...I cooked it on a wire rack, placed on a large cookie sheet, so that heat would get underneath. The result is crispy veggies all over!! It also helped cut down on the cook time by about 15 minutes. Next time I will use less breadcrumbs as this method of cooking brings out the crunch naturally (also, some of the breadcrumbs fell through the rack anyway).  This recipe is going to be a regular for me.

text:
This is so simple and so good, easily modified to add different veg based on what you have on hand, or for me, what you want to use up! The only reason I docked it a star is because I don't think zucchini should go the whole hour... 40 mins MAX, 30 would be better. I did chopped potato, golden beets, carrots, onion tossed in oil & seasoning for 20 minutes, then added the zucchini and an orange pepper, stirred and baked the remaining 40 mins. Next time I'll add after 30 mins, cause it was still a little soft for my taste. Planned to add romano cheese as several reviewers suggested, but I was out, which I didn't realize til right after I returned from the store (of course!) so left that part out, but would have been so much better with it! Leftovers were yummy for lunch today too. A most delicious way to clean out the veg drawer :)

text:
Per other reviewers, I used Panko bread crumbs and sprinkled parmesan flakes after removing dish from the oven.

The potatoes were problematic; I sliced them very thin but they were not cooked through after 1 hour in the oven.  I also cut the squash and peppers in huge chunks, so they were not mushy.  I did not open/stir the dish during baking -- which was fine because the top half of the veggies had a lovely grilled texture.

Next time I will cook the potatoes in the microwave first.

This dish was delicious the next day, reheated.

text:
After reading the instructions, I knew it would take longer for the potatoes to cook than the zucchini.  I followed the recipe exactly but changed one thing.  It was more work but I removed all the zucchini pieces before placing the dish in the oven because I knew the zucchinis would become mush after an hour of cooking.  I should have kept the red peppers out also until about 30 minutes left and added the zucchinis about 20 minutes left in the cooking.

After cooking for 30 minutes, I decided to add the zucchini.  In the end, it tasted ok and the texture was still ok (not mushy for zucchinis) but the pepper was overcooked, too but not as mushy as it could have been.

Next time, I will boil the potatoes halfway through, cut them up to approximately same sizes as the zucchinis and the red peppers.  Bake them all at the same time for no more than 20-25 minutes.

I would make it again but with more garlic and other seasonings because it was a bit bland.

text:
I usually make a recipe as written the first time.  But based on some of the comments, I didn't do that this time.  1.  I increased zucchini and decreased potato.  2.  I cut the zucchini in large chunks but cut the potatos in not-too-thin slices to equalize cooking time.  3.  I added parmesan.  4.  I sauteed some diced onion with 2 cloves of garlic.  5.  Because of the liquid and oil from sauteing the onion and garlic, I reduced the oil to 1/8 C.  6.  Due to the above changes, cooking time was just 30 min.  All that said, it was FABULOUS.  Will definitely make again and again.  Only gave 4 stars because it seemed to need some adjustments; otherwise it would have been 5 stars.

text:
I made this a couple times now.  My family ate this very well.  I followed a few suggestions.  I added extra bread crumbs (I used plain bread crumbs), 1/2 of an onions, 1/2 cup Parmesan cheese, 1 tsp salt, 1/2 tsp pepper, 1 tsp dried granulated garlic, and 1 tsp dried granulated onion.  Once all stirred together I drizzled 2 T margarine over it before baking.  I didn't stir it at all during the baking time and I left it uncovered (it doesn't specify in the recipe).  When it was done I sprinkled some cheddar cheese over it.   It was really good.  
The first time I made this: once it was all baked, I added some hamburger which I cooked with more onions, salt, pepper, onion powder, and minced garlic.  After I mixed in the hamburger, I sprinkled cheddar cheese over it and cooked it under the broiler for a couple minutes.  And that was good, too.

I made this recipe, but it really wasn't anything I haven't made before. My mother is from Greece and we grew up on all sorts of variations on this dish. Generally,  you make it with whatever vegetables you have on hand...zucchini, potatoes, peppers, eggplant, beans, etc. 

I made the recipe pretty much as indicated here, except instead of cutting everything up into chunks, I used my spiralizer. Mainly, just because I wanted to use it.  I liked it because it really stretched the veggies farther and let them crisp up more in the oven. The only addition I made was that I also added oregano for more flavor.  I also used whole wheat breadcrumbs, because that is what I happened to have on hand after my last trip to Whole Foods.

My family loved it. I read other reviews and made a few simple changes but it may have been great as written. I do not like zucchini when it is too soft so I cut potatoes (skin included) into chunks, barely coated with olive oil and cooked about 20 minutes before adding rest of ingredients. Stirred everything together and cooked another 30 minutes or so until everything was cooked but not mushy. I also  used seasoned  Panko instead of bread crumbs since I had some on hand. Will be making this again soon.

This was really good.  The only changes I made was in the way I put it together, and I substituted garlic powder  for the sliced garlic. Really good, but made some modifications. I used Panko instead of plain breadcrumbs. I used red potatoes, leaving the skin on. I added eggplant, a couple handfuls of cherry tomatoes & 1/2 red onion, city into chunks. I used 1 red bell pepper & 1 yellow bell pepper & added 1/2 c grated parmesan cheese. I increased the garlic to 4 cloves (we like a lot of garlic) & increased spices, breadcrumbs & oil to compensate for the added ingredients. To make it a complete meal, I added Great White Northern Beans. It also made a good side dish to some grilled Swai. When I served it with the fish, I changed the paprika to Old Bay seasoning. It was delicious

text:
I am a novice cook, and I found this fairly easy to follow with pleasant results. I used about 1 tbsp more olive oil because it seemed difficult to coat everything, but that may have been unnecessary. 

My only complaint was that the images show significant amounts of bread crumbs on everything, whereas mine was very sparse. This could be because I made my own bread crumbs from dethawed Ezekiel 4:9 bread that I pulverized in my blender, or it could be that I needed to use more bread crumbs.  My idea of "medium" potatoes and zuchinni may be different than what the author means, because this batch would not fit in a "medium" pyrex dish. I had to use the large 9x13 Pyrex - and even then it seemed quite full. Next time I will split it between two Pyrex dishes. 

Finally, I don't think I added enough Paprika because I did not get any peppery taste as other reviewers mention. As a novice, I was very uncertain of how much to add. I will try measuring in the future and recording results. 

All of this aside, I loved how this tasted and devoured it. It's one of the first things I've made that has not come out bland or with any major screw-ups. lol.   Edit: I should note that I used zuchinni and potatoes straight from the farmer's market, so they were very fresh and flavorful!

text:
This recipe was awesome! I just used all the vegetables I had in my garden and refrigerator, here is my variation of this recipe. 3 zucchinis, 3 small and skinny peeled eggplants, 1 tomato (not peeled). Tossed this together, with 3/4 cup plain breadcrumbs, salt, pepper, about 1T and 2t of garlic from a jar (I didn't have fresh garlic), and 1/3 cup olive oil. I put it into a 9x13 pan, and sprinkled a lot of pecorino romano cheese on top. Baked this for 55min, which was slightly too much (next time I will bake it for 45-50min.). It made a dinner that was perfect for five people, I also added some ravioli to my dinner. 
The cheese adds a very good taste, and I would recommend to anyone who is reading this to use it. :)

text:
Everyone in my family ate this- and that's a miracle!  I was concerned about cooking time and seasoning after reading other reviews, but the recipe worked well.  I used 2 garlic cloves (we love garlic), 1 tsp salt, 1/2 tsp paprika, and 1/8 tsp pepper.  We would have liked it as well with 3/4 tsp salt, but it was definitely not bland.  Our zucchini were all small (the last of the season, right before a freeze), so there weren't many seeds- all of the chunks were fairly firm; because they were small, I used 4 or 5 instead of 2 medium.  When we make this next year with larger zucchini, I'll do as another reviewer suggested and cut the seeds out of the center before chunk-ing.  I cut the potatoes fairly small, the zucchini about twice that size.  Other than adding an extra clove of garlic, I followed the recipe exactly.  The bread crumbs gave this dish a great texture- not exactly crunchy, but not soggy, either- just nice and toothsome :)  This is also a beautiful dish.  I enjoyed making it, eating it, and reheating it the next day.  We'll definitely be making this again next summer.

text:
I made these veggies last night to go with a meatloaf (EZ Meatloaf, also from this site), in an effort to use up some extra zucchinis that I had.  I used 2 smallish zucchinis, 6 medium potatoes, and an onion (no red pepper because I didn't have any on hand, and no garlic cloves because sadly, I'm allergic to garlic and can only eat minimal amounts).  I tossed the veggies with the ingredients as directed, using a garlic olive oil to still get some of the garlic flavor, and adding some chili powder. I used panko breadcrumbs, which worked just fine.  This dish turned out well and went great with my meatloaf for a nice homey, fall meal!

What a delicious and hearty recipe! As a college student, this was a wonderful recipe to bake and have ready for myself for the rest of the week! My only suggestion for it is that if you want a less calorie ridden meal then use less potatoes. Next time I make it I'm definitely going to add more zucchini because when zucchini bakes for an hour it tends to get reaaally tiny. So, I'd recommend four zucchinis instead of two. Also, its really hearty, but if you want more of a flavorful POW or tang to your recipe add lime/lemon juice to the veggies or some spice to it!

I cut the potatos small and sliced the zucchini in 1/4 inch slices, added onion. I didn't have any red pepper. I tossed everything with olive oil then added the rest of the ingredients. I also found some broccoli that I had cut from the garden so I added that. It was delicious and everyone loved it! I will make again!!
